<Review>Overall I was satisfied with my experience. The young lady who signed me out was very friendly and helpful. The car was nice, clean, decent size, and in good shape.

However, I do have a few complaints.
I changed my original pick up date but when I called to confirm a pick up, the main res. # had no record of my change. When I texted the gentleman who picked me up ( I believe he was the branch manager) to ask a parking ordinance question, he never replied.

I was not happy with the GM entertainment/info. system in the car. It kept making beeping noises, not sure why. It wouldn't charge my phone. the display kept showing all kinds of odd messages on it about music, and after about an hour, the XM/Sirius satellite stopped playing.

I was fine with that last thing as I didn't ask for that service if it was extra money, but it was odd that it played then stopped. And I couldn't get reception for the excellent LA public radio station I always like to listen to in LA, KCRW-FM.

I was also under the impression I wasn't getting charged for the day I had to pick up the car. I didn't need the car until Labor Day, 9/5, but because the branch was closed that day for the holiday (I do NOT begrudge people getting a holiday off, especially Labor Day), I had to get the car the day before, on Sunday, 9/4.

I never even used the vehicle that day except to drive from the Enterprise office to the hotel I was staying at, where I had to pay $40 to park the car overnight as there is no street parking near where I stayed except for residents with permits. Basically the car cost me an extra $75 for a day I didn't even want or need it (extra day's rental plus hotel parking).

When I called Enterprise to inquire about this when I saw the extra day's charge on my bill, I was told someone would look into it and call me back. Well its now two weeks later and no call back from anyone.

I was planning on not reviewing Enterprise because I didn't want to say anything bad about the company, but now that I've gotten two emails asking me to do so, I figured I would take the time and write my review.

< Review>
Terrible. I came here with my friends for my birthday. I called ahead to make sure that our dogs would be welcome, over the phone they said the dogs were fine and gave us the thumbs up to bring our dogs. When we got there the server would not let us bring our dogs into the room. Even though some other patrons had their dog with them in the room. It was over a hundred degrees that day. So even though it broke up the group we gave it a chance and my husband sat outside with the dogs. The rest of us started our tasting and we were looking around the shop - I found a cute wine coaster and when I picked it up to look for the price the server quickly shouted at me across the bar:  " You have to pay for that you know! " (Totally racially profiling me.) I can't believe how deceptive and rude they were and the wines really aren't that great there's other better friendlier wineries in Santa Ynez I'll never go back.</Review>

None< /pics>

< review>
A tasting manager at another winery recommended Kalyra, and complimented their wines as accessible and tasty.

A trip to this no-frills winery really turned into magic for us - we found the staff friendly and informed, and eager to share both their knowledge and Kalyra's ample selection of very accessible wines. As opposed to wineries with the polo club look, or the survivalist cave thing, Kalyra feels like a beach party with friends.

Tasting sessions usually last about 30 minutes, we stayed for two hours, had lunch petted the cat, joined the wine subscription club, and I took a picture of the parking lot that's my home screen on my phone. It's a good memory that I enjoy every day. I can't wait to go back.< /review>

I am a member of this winery. The view is beautiful from the outside deck. Nice tasting room tiki style. The wine is so amazing. <pics>None</pics>< Rate>
4</Rate>
< Gmap_id>
0x80e9138f7ac1eb17:0xd846d61799faf18e< /Gmap_id>
<date>1520277347313< /date>< review>
Foremost, DART Coffee Co. is a wholesale business. As this is the case we had the opportunity to enjoy their coffee via one of their local Santa Barbara accounts, Helena Bakery, which is a short walk from their roasting facility. Helena's displayed a limited selection of DART Coffee, all of which were from Mexico, Finca La Barranca (that day, of course), and sold bags for $16 per 12oz. As it was drip/batch brew from an account - rather than the roaster themselves - it was difficult to assess the quality of the beans as the roaster intended (hence the 4 stars). We will say that there were obvious chocolate and nutty notes, although that's quite common of the region.

From our experience, we would suggest purchasing bag(s) from DART's website, and home brewing if you have the resources.

Instagram @coffeepourfavor
Found this helpful🤔? 'Like' it 👍 below!
❓ Let us know!

Coffee: Specialty grade from and sourced from local importers including Bodhi Leaf. Roasted, from what we've experienced, medium-dark range for a Central with a heavy Central and South American lineup at the time of this writing.

Equipment: All beans roasted in house on a Diedrich IR-12.

Location: This is a wholesale business with mostly local accounts throughout central CA. It's our understanding that deliveries of coffee purchased via their site may be free for the local SB community.

Final Note:
We're super excited to see more local roasters popping up in Santa Barbara County and look forward to cupping some of DART's other coffees that are available, you should brew too!

☕😆👍< /review>
